       \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > About\n\n\n  \nAbout ICS\n\n\n\n\n\nBy establishing the University of California's first computer science\n            school in 2002, UC Irvine made an investment in the future that reflects\n            its historical commitment to raising the bar of excellence. \nFrom\n                pioneering computer science courses more than three decades ago to\n                the creation of the Donald Bren School of Information and Computer\n                Sciences, UCI continues to be an institute that leads information\n                technology education and research across the globe.              \nThe Bren School  began as a department in 1968. More than 35 years later, it\n                was formally recognized as a school \xe2\x80\x94 and in June 2004, the School\n                adopted benefactor Donald Bren's name in recognition of his generous\n                contribution and visionary leadership.\nAs an independent school focused solely on the computer and information\n            sciences, the Bren School has a unique perspective on the information technology\n            disciplines that allows us a broad foundation from which to build\n            educational programs and research initiatives that explore the many\n            applications of the computing discipline \xe2\x80\x94 from circuits and systems\n            to software engineering and human aspects of computing.\nBuilding on our strong foundation of computer science fundamentals,\n            the Bren School conducts cutting-edge research in strategic areas ideal for collaborative\n            work. \nBy blending research with education in multiple disciplines,\n                the Bren School is leading interdisciplinary efforts in order to meet the challenges\n                of the future.\nOur Mission\nThe Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences aims for excellence in research and education.\nOur mission is to lead the innovation of new information and computing technology by fundamental research in the core areas of information and computer sciences and cultivating authentic, cutting-edge research collaborations across the broad range of computing and information application domains as well as studying their economic, commercial and social significance.\xc2\xa0\nThe diversity of our collaborations serves to reshape domains as far reaching as education, art and entertainment, business and law, the environment and biological systems, health care and medicine.\xc2\xa0\nConsistent with our mission, we are committed to ensuring excellence through inclusion, producing a diverse, educated workforce for advancing technology, stimulating the economy and transferring new technology into the public realm to greatly advance quality of life.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMore about the school breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">About ICS</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p><img alt="Bren School group of faculty and students" height="341" src="../bin/img/photos/ICS-group-About-Us.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="450"/></p>\n<p>By establishing the University of California\'s first computer science\n            school in 2002, UC Irvine made an investment in the future that reflects\n            its historical commitment to raising the bar of excellence. </p>\n<p>From\n                pioneering computer science courses more than three decades ago to\n                the creation of the Donald Bren School of Information and Computer\n                Sciences, UCI continues to be an institute that leads information\n                technology education and research across the globe.              </p>\n<p>The Bren School  began as a department in 1968. More than 35 years later, it\n                was formally recognized as a school &#8212; and in June 2004, the School\n                <a href="bren/index.php">adopted benefactor Donald Bren\'s name in recognition of his generous\n                contribution</a> and visionary leadership.</p>\n<p>As an independent school focused solely on the computer and information\n            sciences, the Bren School has a unique perspective on the information technology\n            disciplines that allows us a broad foundation from which to build\n            educational programs and research initiatives that explore the many\n            applications of the computing discipline &#8212; from circuits and systems\n            to software engineering and human aspects of computing.</p>\n<p>Building on our strong foundation of computer science fundamentals,\n            the Bren School <a href="../faculty/area/index.php">conducts cutting-edge research</a> in strategic areas ideal for collaborative\n            work. </p>\n<p>By blending research with education in multiple disciplines,\n                the Bren School is leading interdisciplinary efforts in order to meet the challenges\n                of the future.</p>\n<h3>Our Mission</h3>\n<p>The Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences aims for excellence in research and education.</p>\n<p>Our mission is to lead the innovation of new information and computing technology by fundamental research in the core areas of information and computer sciences and cultivating authentic, cutting-edge research collaborations across the broad range of computing and information application domains as well as studying their economic, commercial and social significance.&#160;</p>\n<p>The diversity of our collaborations serves to reshape domains as far reaching as education, art and entertainment, business and law, the environment and biological systems, health care and medicine.&#160;</p>\n<p>Consistent with our mission, we are committed to ensuring excellence through inclusion, producing a diverse, educated workforce for advancing technology, stimulating the economy and transferring new technology into the public realm to greatly advance quality of life.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><!-- start right hand side bar -->\n<div id="sidebar_title">More about the school &#187;</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="about_mission.php">Bren ICS Mission</a></li>\n<li><a href="bren/index.php">About the Bren gift</a></li>\n<li><a \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > About\n\n\n  \nWelcome from Dean Stern\n\n\n\n\n\n\nWelcome to the Donald Bren School of Information and\nComputer Sciences (ICS) at UC Irvine. As the only computing-focused school in the University of California\nsystem, the Bren School is a unique place for study, research and collaboration. Our three departments \xe2\x80\x94 Computer\nScience, Informatics and Statistics \xe2\x80\x94 incorporate a broad range of curricular\nand research interests across the informational and computational sciences.\nThe school offers a range of undergraduate majors\n(six in all), including recently developed majors in Computer Game Science and Business Information Management. The diverse selection of majors enables\nstudents to gain in-depth knowledge of the information and computer sciences\nwhile developing an understanding of the broad reach of the discipline. Our goal is to give students the real-world\ntools necessary to succeed in the ever-changing technology industry.\nOur faculty and graduate students are leaders in their research areas which span\ninformation and computer sciences; they obtain corporate and federal extramural\ngrants, they write leading textbooks in their fields, publish influential\njournal articles, and participate in key conferences and workshops.\xc2\xa0 Research in the information and\ncomputer sciences is applicable across many scholarly and scientific fields.\xc2\xa0 Indeed, applications to scientific and\npolicy questions in the biological/health, engineering, and social science\ndisciplines motivate much of our research.\nI invite you to explore our website and learn more about the\nBren School. Please feel free to\ncontact me at icsdean@ics.uci.edu if\nyou have questions or comments.\nThanks,\n\n\n\t\t  Hal SternTed and Janice Smith Family Foundation Dean\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMore about the school breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Welcome from Dean Stern</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<div class="img_caption_left">\n<img alt="Hal S. Stern" height="163" src="../bin/img/heads/halstern.jpg" width="211"/></div>\n<p class="text">Welcome to the Donald Bren School of Information and\nComputer Sciences (ICS) at UC Irvine. As the only computing-focused school in the University of California\nsystem, the Bren School is a unique place for study, research and collaboration. Our three departments &#8212; Computer\nScience, Informatics and Statistics &#8212; incorporate a broad range of curricular\nand research interests across the informational and computational sciences.</p>\n<p class="text">The school offers a range of <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/ugrad/degrees/index.php">undergraduate majors</a>\n(six in all), including recently developed majors in Computer Game Science and Business Information Management. The diverse selection of majors enables\nstudents to gain in-depth knowledge of the information and computer sciences\nwhile developing an understanding of the broad reach of the discipline. Our goal is to give students the real-world\ntools necessary to succeed in the ever-changing technology industry.</p>\n<p class="text">Our faculty and graduate students are leaders in their <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/area/">research areas</a> which span\ninformation and computer sciences; they obtain corporate and federal extramural\ngrants, they write leading textbooks in their fields, publish influential\njournal articles, and participate in key conferences and workshops.&#160; Research in the information and\ncomputer sciences is applicable across many scholarly and scientific fields.&#160; Indeed, applications to scientific and\npolicy questions in the biological/health, engineering, and social science\ndisciplines motivate much of our research.</p>\n<p class="text">I invite you to explore our website and learn more about the\nBren School. Please feel free to\ncontact me at <a href="mailto:icsdean@ics.uci.edu">icsdean@ics.uci.edu</a> if\nyou have questions or comments.</p>\n<p class="text">Thanks,</p>\n<p><img alt="Hal Stern" height="29" src="../bin/img/signature/halsternsig.jpg" width="145"/></p>\n<p>\n\t\t  Hal Stern<br/>Ted and Janice Smith Family Foundation Dean<i><br/></i></p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><!-- start right hand side bar -->\n<div id="sidebar_title">More about the school &#187;</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="about_mission.php">Bren ICS Mission</a></li>\n<li><a \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > About\n\n\n  \nFacts and figures\n\n\n\n\nBREN SCHOOL FACTS\n\nOnly computing-focused school in UC system\nFounded in 1968 as Department of Information and Computer Science\nEstablished in 2002 as an independent school, the Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences (ICS)\n\nRANKINGS\n\nUS News & World ReportBren School rated 29th among computer science graduate programs and 14th among public university programs\xc2\xa0(2014)\nMicrosoft Academic Search website ranking of authors and organizations by citations (as of March 11, 2014)UC Irvine 20th among U.S. universities in computer science.\xc2\xa0Some top subareas:- Human-computer interaction: 4th- Software engineering: 9th- Databases: 8th\n\nBY THE NUMBERS\n\n2,831 students\n78 Faculty (full-time and lecturers)\n48 Staff\n8,000+ Alumni\nThree departments:\xc2\xa0Computer Science,\xc2\xa0Informatics,\xc2\xa0Statistics\n\nUNDERGRADUATE PROGRAM 2,366 undergraduate students in seven majors\n\nComputer Science\nData Science\xc2\xa0(established 2015)\nInformatics\nSoftware Engineering (established 2012)\nComputer Game Science (established 2010)\nBusiness Information Management (joint with the Paul Merage School of Business)\nComputer Science & Engineering (joint with the Henry Samueli School of Engineering)\n\nGRADUATE PROGRAM\n465 graduate students enrolled in Fall 2014-2015\n\nComputer Science:\xc2\xa0Ph.D. 130\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0M.S. 136\nInformatics:\xc2\xa0Ph.D. 42\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2 M.S. 21\nSoftware Engineering:\xc2\xa0Ph.D. 16\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0M.S. 24\nStatistics:\xc2\xa0Ph.D. 29\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0M.S. 30\nNetworked Systems:\xc2\xa0Ph.D. 9\xc2\xa0\xe2\x80\xa2\xc2\xa0M.S. 28\n\n\nINFLUENTIAL FACULTY AND ALUMNI\nOur faculty\n\n1 member of the National Academy of Engineering\n3 Fellows of the American Association for the Advancement of Science (AAAS)\n12 Fellows of the Association for Computing Machinery (ACM)\n6 Fellows of the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers (IEEE)\n3 Fellows of the American Statistical Association (ASA)\n\nOur alumni\n\nRoy Fielding (B.S. '88, M.S. '93, Ph.D. '00) primary architect of HTTP/1.1\nPaul Mockapetris (Ph.D. '82) inventor of the Domain Name System (DNS)\nLarry Rowe (B.S. '70, PhD '76) professor emeritus, UC Berkeley\nBarbara Kew (B.S. '75) CIO of Hill-Rom (medical technology)\nTim Kashani (B.S. '86) CEO of IT Mentors and Tony Award-winning\n\nRESEARCH CENTERS\n\nIntel Science and Technology Center for Social Computing\nInstitute for Genomics and Bioinformatics\nInstitute for Software Research\nInstitute for Virtual Environments and Computer Games\nCenter for Algorithms and Theory of Computation\nCenter for Emergency Response Technologies\nCenter for Machine Learning and Intelligent Systems\nLaboratory for Ubiquitous Computing and Interaction\xc2\xa0\nSecure Computing and Networking Center\n\nSTUDENT ORGANIZATIONS\n\nACM (Association for Computing Machinery) - UC Irvine Chapter\nDesign Art and Technology Makerspace (DAT space)\nGraduate Women in Computer Science (GWICS)\nICS Student Council (ICSSC)\nManagement Information Student Society (MAISS)\nWomen in Information and Computer Sciences (WICS)\nVideo Game Development Club (VGDC)\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMore about the school \xc2\xbb\n\nBren ICS Mission\nAbout the Bren gift\nDean's welcome\nBren School id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Facts and figures</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<strong>BREN SCHOOL FACTS</strong><br/>\n<ul>\n<li>Only computing-focused school in UC system</li>\n<li>Founded in 1968 as Department of Information and Computer Science</li>\n<li>Established in 2002 as an independent school, the Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences (ICS)</li>\n</ul>\n<strong>RANKINGS</strong>\n<ul>\n<li><em>US News &amp; World Report<br/></em>Bren School rated 29th among computer science graduate programs and 14th among public university programs&#160;(2014)</li>\n<li><em>Microsoft Academic Search</em> website ranking of authors and organizations by citations (as of March 11, 2014)<br/>UC Irvine 20th among U.S. universities in computer science.&#160;Some top subareas:<br/>- Human-computer interaction: 4th<br/>- Software engineering: 9th<br/>- Databases: 8th</li>\n</ul>\n<strong>BY THE NUMBERS</strong>\n<ul>\n<li>2,831 students</li>\n<li>78 Faculty (full-time and lecturers)</li>\n<li>48 Staff</li>\n<li>8,000+ Alumni</li>\n<li>Three departments:&#160;<a href="../../computerscience/index.php">Computer Science</a>,&#160;<a href="http://www.informatics.uci.edu/">Informatics</a>,&#160;<a href="../../statistics/index.php">Statistics</a></li>\n</ul>\n<strong>UNDERGRADUATE PROGRAM</strong> <br/><br/>2,366 undergraduate students in seven majors\n<ul>\n<li>Computer Science</li>\n<li>Data Science&#160;(established 2015)</li>\n<li>Informatics</li>\n<li>Software Engineering (established 2012)</li>\n<li>Computer Game Science (established 2010)</li>\n<li>Business Information Management (joint with the Paul Merage School of Business)</li>\n<li>Computer Science &amp; Engineering (joint with the Henry Samueli School of Engineering)</li>\n</ul>\n<strong>GRADUATE </strong><strong>PROGRAM</strong>\n<p>465 graduate students enrolled in Fall 2014-2015</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Computer Science:&#160;Ph.D. 130&#160;&#8226;&#160;M.S. 136</li>\n<li>Informatics:&#160;Ph.D. 42&#160;&#8226; M.S. 21</li>\n<li>Software Engineering:&#160;Ph.D. 16&#160;&#8226;&#160;M.S. 24</li>\n<li>Statistics:&#160;Ph.D. 29&#160;&#8226;&#160;M.S. 30</li>\n<li>Networked Systems:&#160;Ph.D. 9&#160;&#8226;&#160;M.S. 28</li>\n</ul>\n<style><!--\n#grad_table TABLE,TD { border: 0px solid grey; padding-right: 1em; }\n--></style>\n<p><strong>INFLUENTIAL FACULTY AND ALUMNI</strong></p>\n<p><em><strong>Our faculty</strong></em></p>\n<ul>\n<li>1 member of the National Academy of Engineering</li>\n<li>3 Fellows of the American Association for the Advancement of Science (AAAS)</li>\n<li>12 Fellows of the Association for Computing Machinery (ACM)</li>\n<li>6 Fellows of the Institute of Electrical and Electronics Engineers (IEEE)</li>\n<li>3 Fellows of the American Statistical Association (ASA)</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em><strong>Our alumni</strong></em></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Roy Fielding (B.S. \'88, M.S. \'93, Ph.D. \'00) primary architect of HTTP/1.1</li>\n<li>Paul Mockapetris (Ph.D. \'82) inventor of the Domain Name System (DNS)</li>\n<li>Larry Rowe (B.S. \'70, PhD \'76) professor emeritus, UC Berkeley</li>\n<li>Barbara Kew (B.S. \'75) CIO of Hill-Rom (medical technology)</li>\n<li>Tim Kashani (B.S. \'86) CEO of IT Mentors and Tony Award-winning</li>\n</ul>\n<strong>RESEARCH CENTERS</strong><br/>\n<ul>\n<li>Intel Science and Technology Center for Social Computing</li>\n<li>Institute for Genomics and Bioinformatics</li>\n<li>Institute for Software Research</li>\n<li>Institute for Virtual Environments and Computer Games</li>\n<li>Center for Algorithms and Theory of Computation</li>\n<li>Center for Emergency Response Technologies</li>\n<li>Center for Machine Learning and Intelligent Systems</li>\n<li>Laboratory for Ubiquitous Computing and Interaction&#160;</li>\n<li>Secure Computing and Networking Center</li>\n</ul>\n<strong>STUDENT ORGANIZATIONS<br/></strong>\n<ul>\n<li>ACM (Association for Computing Machinery) - UC Irvine Chapter</li>\n<li>Design Art and Technology Makerspace (DAT space)</li>\n<li>Graduate Women in Computer Science (GWICS)</li>\n<li>ICS Student Council (ICSSC)</li>\n<li>Management Information Student Society (MAISS)</li>\n<li>Women in Information and Computer Sciences (WICS)</li>\n<li>Video Game Development Club (VGDC)</li>\n</ul>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><!-- start \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > About > Donald Bren Hall\n\n\n  \nDonald Bren Hall\n\n\n\n\n\t\t  \nThe six-story Donald Bren Hall  expanded the existing Bren School campus and increased general assignment classroom space by more than 90,800 square feet. \nThe design of this facility is intended to enhance interaction between faculty and students and to create a progressive learning environment. \nDesigned with flexibility in mind, the building  accommodates the Bren School's  growing faculty, staff and student populations. \nThe first classes in Donald Bren Hall were held Jan. 5, 2007; the Dean's office moved in on Jan. 8, 2007. \nOn June 20, Donald Bren Hall was offically dedicated during a morning ceremony which was attended by Donald Bren, former Dean Debra J. Richardson, Chancellor Michael Drake and about 400 campus and community guests.\nAn open house followed the ceremony, allowing the on-campus and off-campus community a rare sneak peek into the school's  various research projects and their global impact on everyday lives. \nDonald Bren Hall accommodates: \n\nMore than 125 faculty offices\n90 research labs, wet labs and/or offices\n10 classrooms (from 30-seat to 65-seat)\n250-seat lecture hall\n125-seat lecture hall\n2 50-seat lecture hall\nDean's office/administrative support\nDepartmental offices\nBren School  staff offices/facilities\n\nCeremonial groundbreaking on Donald Bren Hall took place on June 9, 2004. Visitors can view the groundbreaking press release as well as photos from the groundbreaking ceremony, attended by the building's namesake, philanthropist and chairman of The Irvine Company, Donald Bren.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMore about the school \xc2\xbb\n\nBren ICS Mission\nAbout the Bren gift\nDean's welcome\nBren School Intranet\n\nDonald Bren Hall\nUndergraduate education\nGraduate studies\nFind breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/brenhall/">Donald Bren Hall</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/brenhall/">Donald Bren Hall</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Donald Bren Hall</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p align="center"><img alt="artist rendering of bren hall" height="138" src="../../bin/img/photos/buildings/ics3.jpg" width="300"/>\t\t  </p>\n<p>The six-story Donald Bren Hall  expanded the existing Bren School campus and increased general assignment classroom space by more than 90,800 square feet. </p>\n<p>The design of this facility is intended to enhance interaction between faculty and students and to create a progressive learning environment. </p>\n<p>Designed with flexibility in mind, the building  accommodates the Bren School\'s  growing faculty, staff and student populations. </p>\n<p>The first classes in Donald Bren Hall were held Jan. 5, 2007; the Dean\'s office moved in on Jan. 8, 2007. </p>\n<p><a href="../../community/events/openhouse/dedication.html">On June 20, Donald Bren Hall was offically dedicated</a> during a morning ceremony which was attended by Donald Bren, former Dean Debra J. Richardson, Chancellor Michael Drake and about 400 campus and community guests.</p>\n<p>An open house followed the ceremony, allowing the on-campus and off-campus community a rare sneak peek into the school\'s  various research projects and their global impact on everyday lives. </p>\n<p>Donald Bren Hall accommodates: </p>\n<ul>\n<li>More than 125 faculty offices</li>\n<li>90 research labs, wet labs and/or offices</li>\n<li>10 classrooms (from 30-seat to 65-seat)</li>\n<li>250-seat lecture hall</li>\n<li>125-seat lecture hall</li>\n<li>2 50-seat lecture hall</li>\n<li>Dean\'s office/administrative support</li>\n<li>Departmental offices</li>\n<li>Bren School  staff offices/facilities</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Ceremonial groundbreaking on Donald Bren Hall took place on June 9, 2004. Visitors can view the <strong><a href="../bren/bren_press.php">groundbreaking press release</a></strong> as well as <strong><a href="../bren/bren_press.php">photos from the groundbreaking ceremony</a></strong>, attended by the building\'s namesake, philanthropist and chairman of The Irvine Company, Donald Bren.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><!-- start right hand side bar -->\n<div id="sidebar_title">More about the school &#187;</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="../about_mission.php">Bren ICS Mission</a></li>\n<li><a href="../bren/index.php">About the Bren         will substitute for an in-person visit.\n\nThe Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences (ICS) is\n            the first and only computer science school in the University of California,\n            offering\n            visitors opportunities to attend academic lectures, interact with\n            leading computer science researchers and recruit intelligent and\n          out of the box thinking computer science students.\nIf you're interested\n          in attending ICS and want to learn more about a particular degree program\n          - even\n            meet with faculty doing research that piques your interest - please call the Student Affairs Office at (949) 824-5156 and ask to speak to an undergraduate or graduate counselor.  \n Campus walking tours are offered almost every Monday through Friday. Please check the Tour Calendar for available times and to ensure that there is a tour offered on the day you wish to visit.\nDirections to the Bren School\n            \xc2\xbb From LAX (42 miles from UCI)\n            \xc2\xbb From John Wayne (5 miles from UCI)\n            \xc2\xbb From major freeways (405, 73, 55, 5)\nCampus Map\n            \xc2\xbb Campus map of UCI (PDF) \n          The Bren School Student Affairs Office has relocated to: Information and Computer Science, Suite 352 (building #302 on the campus map).\nParking\n            \xc2\xbb UCI guest parking information\n\n\n\n\n\n\nMore about the school \xc2\xbb\n\nBren ICS Mission\nAbout the Bren gift\nDean's welcome\nBren School Intranet\n\nDonald Bren Hall\nUndergraduate education\nGraduate studies\nFind faculty and staff\nContact us\niTunes U\nSafety procedures\nVisit the Bren School\n\n\n\nUseful links \xc2\xbb\n\nLocal traffic report\nLocal weather forecast\nLocal bus routes\nAMTRAK\nMapquest\n\n\n   \n   Quick Links \n      \n      \n\n\n\n         \n      \n         \n      \n         \n      \n         \n      \n         \n\n\nCopyright Inquiries |\n   UCI Directory |\n   Intranet |\n   \n   \n \n  icswebmaster\n\n\n\n\n", 'html': '<html xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml">\n<head>\n                <title>Visit Us @ the Donald Bren School of Information &amp; Computer Sciences</title>\n                <meta content="Learn more about visiting UCI\'s Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences. href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/">About</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/about/visit/">Visit the bren school</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Visit ICS</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<br/><img alt="Information and computer science buildings at UCI" height="244" src="../../bin/img/photos/buildings/BrenBuildings-vistus2015.jpg" width="450"/><br/>\n<br/>\n<p>We can offer virtual tours, pictorials and viewbooks but nothing\n          will substitute for an in-person visit.\n</p>\n<p>The Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences (ICS) is\n            the first and only computer science school in the University of California,\n            offering\n            visitors opportunities to attend academic lectures, interact with\n            leading computer science researchers and recruit intelligent and\n          out of the box thinking computer science students.</p>\n<p>If you\'re interested\n          in attending ICS and want to learn more about a particular degree program\n          - even\n            meet with faculty doing research that piques your interest - please call the Student Affairs Office at (949) 824-5156 and ask to speak to an undergraduate or graduate counselor.  </p>\n<p> Campus walking tours are offered almost every Monday through Friday. Please check the <a href="http://www.campustours.uci.edu/calendar.html">Tour Calendar</a> for available times and to ensure that there is a tour offered on the day you wish to visit.</p>\n<p><strong>Directions to the Bren School</strong><br/>\n            <span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> <a href="visit_fromLAX.php"><strong>From LAX</strong></a> (42 miles from UCI)<br/>\n            <span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> <a href="visit_fromjwa.php"><strong>From John Wayne</strong></a> (5 miles from UCI)<br/>\n            <span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> <a href="visit_fromfreeway.php"><strong>From major freeways</strong></a> (405, 73, 55, 5)</p>\n<p><strong>Campus Map</strong><br/>\n            <span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> <a href="http://communications.uci.edu//documents/pdf/UCI_14_map_campus.pdf"><strong>Campus map of UCI (PDF) </strong></a><br/>\n          The Bren School Student Affairs Office has relocated to: Information and Computer Science, Suite 352 (building #302 on the campus map).</p>\n<p><strong>Parking</strong><br/>\n            <span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> <a href="http://www.parking.uci.edu/permits/"><strong>UCI guest parking information</strong></a></p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > About > \n\n\n  \nEquity & Diversity\n\n\n\n\nMessage from the ICS equity advisor \n\nThe UC Irvine campus is committed to supporting gender equity and diversity. There has never been a more important time to consider diversity in the STEM (science, technology, engineering and math) fields. The field of computer science is changing rapidly, and an academic body with a diverse background can contribute unique ideas and perspectives to the creative development and study of new technologies for a global world. One of the ways we can achieve a more inclusive climate is to educate ourselves on the importance of diversity in our field. To this end, I will use this site to assemble articles that relate to issues concerning women and underrepresented minorities regarding educational achievement, advancement, pay inequity and other topics. If you have any questions regarding our equity program, or if you'd like to suggest articles for posting on this site, please send a message to advance@ics.uci.edu.\n\nI hope you enjoy learning more about this important topic as I have. \n\n\nYour ICS equity advisor,Gloria Mark\n\xc2\xa0\n\nHow ICS compares to the rest of the nation\n\nHere\xe2\x80\x99s how ICS compares with the rest of the country on gender equity in terms of degrees awarded and faculty gender ratio. Data is taken from the 2013-2014 CRA Taulbee Survey.\n\n\xc2\xa0\n\n\n\n\nDegree recipients: nationwide (2013-2014)\n\n      \n\n\n\n            \xc2\xa0\n         \n\nMale\n\n         \nFemale\n\n id="content_title">Equity &amp; Diversity</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<h3><img alt="Some of the 30+ students who earned their Ph.D. from the Bren School in AY 2010-11." height="216" src="Commencement.jpg" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="360"/><br/><br/>Message from the ICS equity advisor </h3>\n<p>\nThe UC Irvine campus is committed to supporting gender equity and diversity. There has never been a more important time to consider diversity in the STEM (science, technology, engineering and math) fields. The field of computer science is changing rapidly, and an academic body with a diverse background can contribute unique ideas and perspectives to the creative development and study of new technologies for a global world. One of the ways we can achieve a more inclusive climate is to educate ourselves on the importance of diversity in our field. To this end, I will use this site to assemble articles that relate to issues concerning women and underrepresented minorities regarding educational achievement, advancement, pay inequity and other topics. If you have any questions regarding our equity program, or if you\'d like to suggest articles for posting on this site, please send a message to <a href="mailto:advance@ics.uci.edu">advance@ics.uci.edu</a>.</p>\n<p>\nI hope you enjoy learning more about this important topic as I have. \n</p>\n<p>\nYour ICS equity advisor,<br/>Gloria Mark</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<hr/>\n<h3>How ICS compares to the rest of the nation</h3>\n<p>\nHere&#8217;s how ICS compares with the rest of the country on gender equity in terms of degrees awarded and faculty gender ratio. Data is taken from the 2013-2014 <a href="http://cra.org//uploads/documents/resources/crndocs/2014-Taulbee-Survey.pdf" target="_blank">CRA Taulbee Survey</a>.</p>\n<style>\n   TABLE.advance class="advance">\n<tbody>\n<tr>\n<td>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n</td>\n<th>\n<p>Male</p>\n</th>\n<th>\n<p>Female</p>\n</th>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>\n<p>Assistant</p>\n</th>\n<td>\n<p>74.2%</p>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>25.8%</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>\n<p>Associate</p>\n</th>\n<td>\n<p>84.1%</p>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>15.9%</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<th>\n<p>Full</p>\n</th>\n<td>\n<p>87.4%</p>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>12.6%</p>\n</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody>\n</table>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Departments\n\n\n  \nDepartments\n\n\n\n\nThe Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences is comprised of three departments that teach the broad foundation of each discipline but allow students the flexibility to explore many areas of computer science with carefully crafted curriculums that appeal to students\xe2\x80\x99 diverse interests.\nComputer Science Department\n  \nThe Department of Computer Science engages in the full spectrum of intellectual activity in computer science, ranging from fundamental theoretical principles, to design and analysis of computer systems and networks, to new and exciting applications in areas as diverse as bioinformatics and computer security.\n\n\nInformatics Department \nThe Department of Informatics focuses on the interdisciplinary study of the design, application, use and impacts of information technology.\n  \n  \n  Statistics Department\n\nThe new Department of Statistics, which officially joined ICS in July 2003, has core strength in statistical theory with a focus on statistical methods for solving interdisciplinary problems.\n\n\n\n\n\n\nCopyright Inquiries |\n   UCI Directory |\n   Intranet |\n   \n   \n \n  icswebmaster |\nUpdated: \nJune 11 2012\n\n\n\n\n", 'html': '<html -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Departments</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\nThe Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences is comprised of three departments that teach the broad foundation of each discipline but allow students the flexibility to explore many areas of computer science with carefully crafted curriculums that appeal to students&#8217; diverse interests.\n<p><b><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/computerscience">Computer Science Department</a></b>\n  <br/>\nThe Department of Computer Science engages in the full spectrum of intellectual activity in computer science, ranging from fundamental theoretical principles, to design and analysis of computer systems and networks, to new and exciting applications in areas as diverse as bioinformatics and computer security.\n<br/>\n<br/>\n<b><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/informatics/">Informatics Department</a></b> <br/>\nThe Department of Informatics focuses on the interdisciplinary study of the design, application, use and impacts of information technology.\n  <br/>\n  <br/>\n  <b><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/statistics">Statistics Department</a></b>\n<br/>\nThe new Department of Statistics, which officially joined ICS in July 2003, has core strength in statistical theory with a focus on statistical methods for solving interdisciplinary problems.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"></div>\n<div id="footer"><a        \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Faculty > Research areas\n\n\n  \nICS Research Areas\n\n\n\n\nCuriosity about the world and a commitment to solving problems are the passions that drive ICS faculty. Their research in the information and computer sciences are applicable to many scholarly and scientific fields. But our faculty don't do it alone, students work side-by-side with nationally renowned professors to advance knowledge and improve lives. Below is a list of ICS research areas:\nAlgorithms and Complexity Bren School faculty members have made significant contributions to many topics in this field, including graph algorithms and graph drawing (computing with systems of pairwise interactions between objects such as web page links, protein interactions, or social networks) and computational geometry (computing with planar or spatial data).\nArtificial Intelligence and Machine Learning Research in AI is concerned with producing machines to automate tasks requiring intelligent behavior. Examples include computer vision, bioinformatics, constraint-based problem solving, text understanding, data mining and smart sensor networks.\nBiomedical Informatics and Computational Biology  Involves the use of techniques from applied mathematics, informatics, statistics, and computer science to solve biological problems. Current areas of research at the Bren School include medical information access and knowledge representation for health-care guidelines.\nComputer Architecture and Design Develops methods and tools for ensuring the reliability and quality of complex, large-scale software systems. These methods and tools support the development, deployment, maintenance and evolution of complex software systems.\nComputer Graphics and Visualization Focuses on the field of visual computing that deals with generating/capturing, representing, rendering and interacting with synthetic and real-world images and video. We work on end-to-end solutions from capturing of images and geometry; representing large geometric, image, and video data sets; geometry and image processing; interactive access and rendering of large visual data sets; algorithms for building large area immersive displays for the presentation of visual content; and interation techniques in both small personal displays and in large displays for collaborative environments.\nComputer-Supported Cooperative Work Information technologies bring people together -- through social networking, through collaborative systems, through digital media, and through communications. Informatics has been a long-term leader in the study of social engagement through information systems. Topics include distance collaboration, workflow and process-based systems, multi-user gaming, and cultural engagements.\nComputer Vision Computer vision at UCI focuses on understanding the information processing capabilities of biological visual systems and on developing computational systems for processing visual media. Research spans both theoretical questions of perception and object representation as well as practical applications ranging from automated surveillance to biological image analysis.\xc2\xa0\nDatabases and Data Mining Focuses on research related to architectures, index structures, algorithms, models, and performance evaluation of a variety of next-generation databases and information systems and technologies for data mining.\nEmbedded Systems Focuses on issues relating to embedded systems, a special-purpose system in which software and hardware computing elements are completely encapsulated by the device or environment it controls. Unlike a general-purpose computer, such as a personal computer, an embedded system performs pre-defined tasks, usually under very specific constraints (e.g, low power) and requirements (e.g., reliability).\xc2\xa0\nEnvironmental Informatics Humanity is currently facing a range of significant environmental challenges such as global warming, species extinction, pollution, and overpopulation. Informatics tools and techniques can help facilitate responses to these challenges, and assist with planning for future environmental issues.\xc2\xa0\nHuman Computer Interaction HCI research at UCI stretches from the architecture of novel interactive systems to the social and cultural considerations of information technology adoption and use. We employ laboratory, ethnographic, and prototyping techniques to understand how people adopt, adapt, and respond to information systems. Recent research has investigated privacy issues in mobile systems, tangible interfaces for group awareness, interactive animation, and visualization of location information.\xc2\xa0\nMedical Informatics This topic concerns the development and application of information systems to healthcare. Information systems have a critical role to play in contemporary health and wellness programs. This includes technology in hospital settings but also persuasive technologies for healthy living, health care in the home and in the community, and in the interactions between partners in the health care system.\xc2\xa0\nMultimedia Computing Multimedia computing started receiving attention more than a decade ago.\xc2\xa0 Naturally, early systems dealt with very limited aspect of multimedia.\xc2\xa0 With progress in technology, several computing addresses important issues in creation, communication, storage, access, and presentation of information and experiences.\xc2\xa0 In our department, we are addressing research issues in fundamentals of multimedia systems and their advanced applications.\xc2\xa0\nNetworks and Distributed Systems Researchers investigate various issues in the design and analysis of high-speed networks for multimedia applications. They are actively involved in research on computer networks and distributed systems, with the goal of designing, analyzing and implementing communication systems that allow high-speed transport of multimedia information between end-users.\xc2\xa0\nOperating Systems\xc2\xa0The operating systems area at UCI embraces a wide range of topics related to theory and practice of computer systems software. Researchers here are building systems for reliable and efficient big data processing, mobile I/O virtualization, program analyses and various other applications.\nProgramming Languages and Systems Systems software research at UCI has expanded to include topics such as program restructuring and transformation techniques for parallelization and distribution, compiler-assisted memory management, component-oriented languages and dynamic code optimization.\xc2\xa0\nScientific and Numerical Computing Refers to the application of computers to scientific problems, from astrophysics to zoology. The mode of application can be system modelling, data analysis and mining, or visualization. The focus can be on developing new computational techniques, such as parallel algorithms or new data mining ideas, or on the novel application of existing techniques to new scientific problems.\nSecurity, Privacy and Cryptography Bren School research in this area includes anonymity and authentication in network security, key agreement and digital signatures in cryptography, and security issues in electronic commerce.\nSocial Informatics UC Irvine is an acknowledged center for the study of social informatics, which incorporates the social and cultural aspects of information technology development and use. Social informatics employs techniques and theories from social sciences and cultural studies to understand the shaping and applications of digital media and their organizational, political, historical, and economic contexts. This topic links information system analysis with design.\nSoftware Engineering Software research at UCI is aimed at creating new software technology and solutions, furthering the information revolution. The central goal of this research is improvement in software development, evolution, deployment, quality, understandability and cost-effectiveness.\nStatistics and Statistical Theory Researchers at UCI are concerned with developing and studying methods for collecting, analyzing, interpreting and presenting empirical data. Statistical principles and methods are important for addressing questions in public policy, medicine, industry and virtually every branch of science.\nUbiquitous Computing Ubiquitous computing builds upon and unites virtually all of thfe current research strengths in the Bren School. Researchers are addressing issues such as context-aware computing, whereby mobile computing responds to one's current context.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore faculty \xc2\xbb\n\nResearch areas\nResearch centers\nResearch highlights\n\nQuick Links \n           \n\nCopyright Inquiries |\n   UCI Directory |\n   Intranet |\n   \n   \n \n  icswebmaster\n\n\n\n\n", 'html': '<html <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/">Faculty</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/area/">Research areas</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/">Faculty</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/area/">Research areas</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">ICS Research Areas</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p><img alt="student conducting research" class="left" height="187" src="../../bin/img/photos/ics_areas_index.jpg" width="200"/>Curiosity about the world and a commitment to solving problems are the passions that drive ICS faculty. Their research in the information and computer sciences are applicable to many scholarly and scientific fields. But our faculty don\'t do it alone, students work side-by-side with nationally renowned professors to advance knowledge and improve lives. Below is a list of ICS research areas:</p>\n<p><a href="area_algorithms.php">Algorithms and Complexity</a><br/> Bren School faculty members have made significant contributions to many topics in this field, including graph algorithms and graph drawing (computing with systems of pairwise interactions between objects such as web page links, protein interactions, or social networks) and computational geometry (computing with planar or spatial data).</p>\n<p><a href="area_ai.php">Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning</a><br/> Research in AI is concerned with producing machines to automate tasks requiring intelligent behavior. Examples include computer vision, bioinformatics, constraint-based problem solving, text understanding, data mining and smart sensor networks.</p>\n<p><a href="area_biomed.php">Biomedical Informatics and Computational Biology</a> <br/> Involves the use of techniques from applied mathematics, informatics, statistics, and computer science to solve biological problems. Current areas of research at the Bren School include medical information access and knowledge representation for health-care guidelines.</p>\n<p><a href="area_compdesign.php">Computer Architecture and Design</a><br/> Develops methods and tools for ensuring the reliability and quality of complex, large-scale software systems. These methods and tools support the development, deployment, maintenance and evolution of complex software systems.</p>\n<p><a href="area_compgraphics.php">Computer Graphics and Visualization</a><br/> Focuses on the field of visual computing that deals with generating/capturing, representing, rendering and interacting with synthetic and real-world images and video. We work on end-to-end solutions from capturing of images and geometry; representing large geometric, image, and video data sets; geometry and image processing; interactive access and rendering of large visual data sets; algorithms for building large area immersive displays for the presentation of visual content; and interation techniques in both small personal displays and in large displays for collaborative environments.</p>\n<p><a href="area_cscw.php">Computer-Supported Cooperative Work</a><br/> Information technologies bring people together -- through social networking, through collaborative systems, through digital media, and through communications. Informatics has been a long-term leader in the study of social engagement through information systems. Topics include distance collaboration, workflow and process-based systems, multi-user gaming, and cultural engagements.</p>\n<p><a href="area_vision.php">Computer Vision<br/> </a>Computer vision at UCI focuses on understanding the information processing capabilities of biological visual systems and on developing computational systems for processing visual media. Research spans both theoretical questions of perception and object representation as well as practical applications ranging from automated surveillance to biological image analysis.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_data.php">Databases and Data Mining</a><br/> Focuses on research related to architectures, index structures, algorithms, models, and performance evaluation of a variety of next-generation databases and information systems and technologies for data mining.</p>\n<p><a href="area_embedded.php">Embedded Systems</a><br/> Focuses on issues relating to embedded systems, a special-purpose system in which software and hardware computing elements are completely encapsulated by the device or environment it controls. Unlike a general-purpose computer, such as a personal computer, an embedded system performs pre-defined tasks, usually under very specific constraints (e.g, low power) and requirements (e.g., reliability).&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_environmental.php">Environmental Informatics</a><br/> Humanity is currently facing a range of significant environmental challenges such as global warming, species extinction, pollution, and overpopulation. Informatics tools and techniques can help facilitate responses to these challenges, and assist with planning for future environmental issues.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_hci.php">Human Computer Interaction</a><br/> HCI research at UCI stretches from the architecture of novel interactive systems to the social and cultural considerations of information technology adoption and use. We employ laboratory, ethnographic, and prototyping techniques to understand how people adopt, adapt, and respond to information systems. Recent research has investigated privacy issues in mobile systems, tangible interfaces for group awareness, interactive animation, and visualization of location information.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_medical.php">Medical Informatics</a><br/> This topic concerns the development and application of information systems to healthcare. Information systems have a critical role to play in contemporary health and wellness programs. This includes technology in hospital settings but also persuasive technologies for healthy living, health care in the home and in the community, and in the interactions between partners in the health care system.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_multimedia.php">Multimedia Computing</a><br/> Multimedia computing started receiving attention more than a decade ago.&#160; Naturally, early systems dealt with very limited aspect of multimedia.&#160; With progress in technology, several computing addresses important issues in creation, communication, storage, access, and presentation of information and experiences.&#160; In our department, we are addressing research issues in fundamentals of multimedia systems and their advanced applications.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_network.php">Networks and Distributed Systems</a><br/> Researchers investigate various issues in the design and analysis of high-speed networks for multimedia applications. They are actively involved in research on computer networks and distributed systems, with the goal of designing, analyzing and implementing communication systems that allow high-speed transport of multimedia information between end-users.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_os.php">Operating Systems</a>&#160;<br/><span>The operating systems area at UCI embraces a wide range of topics related to theory and practice of computer systems software. Researchers here are building systems for reliable and efficient big data processing, mobile I/O virtualization, program analyses and various other applications.</span></p>\n<p><a href="area_systems.php">Programming Languages and Systems</a><br/> Systems software research at UCI has expanded to include topics such as program restructuring and transformation techniques for parallelization and distribution, compiler-assisted memory management, component-oriented languages and dynamic code optimization.&#160;</p>\n<p><a href="area_scientific.php">Scientific and Numerical Computing</a><br/> Refers to the application of computers to scientific problems, from astrophysics to zoology. The mode of application can be system modelling, data analysis and mining, or visualization. The focus can be on developing new computational techniques, such as parallel algorithms or new data mining ideas, or on the novel application of existing techniques to new scientific problems.</p>\n<p><a href="area_security.php">Security, Privacy and Cryptography</a><br/> Bren School research in this area includes anonymity and authentication in network security, key agreement and digital signatures in cryptography, and security issues in electronic commerce.</p>\n<p><a href="area_social.php">Social Informatics</a><br/> UC Irvine is an acknowledged center for the study of social informatics, which incorporates the social and cultural aspects of information technology development and use. Social informatics employs techniques and theories from social sciences and cultural studies to understand the shaping and applications of digital media and their organizational, political, historical, and economic contexts. This topic links information system analysis with design.</p>\n<p><a href="area_software.php">Software Engineering</a><br/> Software research at UCI is aimed at creating new software technology and solutions, furthering the information revolution. The central goal of this research is improvement in software development, evolution, deployment, quality, understandability and cost-effectiveness.</p>\n<p><a href="area_stats.php">Statistics and Statistical Theory</a><br/> Researchers at UCI are concerned with developing and studying methods for collecting, analyzing, interpreting and presenting empirical data. Statistical principles and methods are important for addressing questions in public policy, medicine, industry and virtually every branch of science.</p>\n<p><a href="area_ubi.php">Ubiquitous Computing</a><br/> Ubiquitous computing builds upon and unites virtually all of thfe current research strengths in the Bren School. Researchers are addressing issues such as context-aware computing, whereby mobile computing responds to one\'s current context.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div        \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Faculty > Research centers\n\n\n  \nICS Research Centers\n\n\n\n\n\nOrganized research programs provide a mechanism and organizational structure within which collective research activities can take place that are fundamentally different from those that occur normally within the schools and departments. They are intended to foster the development of short- and long-term research programs that span disciplines and academic units, thereby making it possible for faculty to acquire extramural resources for which they might not otherwise qualify. The following is a list of the research centers that are part of ICS:\nABRC - Ada Byron Research Center  ABRC studies and promotes diverse access to and participation in computer science, engineering, digital media and related information technology fields.\nCalit2 - California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology  A multidisciplinary research institute in collaboration with UCSD, Calit2@UCI integrates academic research with industry experience to seek innovative IT approaches that will benefit society and ignite economic development.\nCDT - Center for Digital TransformationOne of the world's leading think tanks on the impact of information technology on organizations and society and on the management of information technology.\nCenter for Algorithms and Theory of Computation  The goal of research in theoretical computer science is to produce results, supported by rigorous proof, about problems dealing with computers and their applications.\nCenter for Embedded Computer Systems  Conducting leading-edge interdisciplinary research in embedded systems, the center develops innovative design methodologies, and promote technology and knowledge transfer for the benefit of the individual and society.\nCenter for Machine Learning and Intelligent Systems  Addresses the challenges of the modern data-driven world, using computer algorithms to discover useful information from vast data archives.\n \nCenter for Social ComputingConducts foundational research into the relationship between information technology and society. Based at UCI, the center brings together an interdisciplinary group of researchers from leading U.S. universities.\n \nCERT - Center for Emergency Response Technologies  Works to radically transform the ability of responding organizations to gather, manage, use, and disseminate information within emergency response networks and to the general public. By using more robust information systems, response can focus on activities that have the highest potential to save lives and property.\nCOR - Center for Organizational Research  COR contributes to the development of organization theory by connecting scholars from many disciplines who bring their knowledge and methods to a common understanding of these issues.\nCPCC - Center for Pervasive Communications and Computing  Dedicated to serving the vision of wearable computers with wireless connections that enable anyone to have continuous voice, video, and data connectivity.\nComputational Vision Lab The Computational Vision Lab focuses on understanding the information processing capabilities of biological visual systems and on developing computational systems for processing visual media.\nIGB - Institute for Genomics and BioInformatics  Fostering innovative basic and applied research in genomics and BioInformatics, IGB works with established companies, start-ups, government agencies and standards bodies to develop and transition these technologies to widespread and practical application.\nISR - Institute for Software Research  Works toward advancing software and information technology through research partnerships and educating the next generation of software researchers and practitioners in advanced software technologies.\n \nIVECG - Institute for Virtual Environments and Computer Games Brings together researchers for the common goal of understanding and creating technology and applications that transform how we: see the world through immersive visualization and virtual tours; interact and socialize with global communities; communicate and collaborate with colleagues in virtual collaborative space; provide medical care and training to remote corners of the world; and educate all ages and populations using virtual environments.\n \nLUCI - Laboratory for Ubiquitous Computing and Interaction  Addresses the entire range of research problems that arise from the ubiquitous computing vision: the design of novel devices, the structure of software systems, techniques for designing and building systems, patterns of interaction, and the cultural implications of ubiquitous computing.\nSecure Systems and Software Laboratory  The Secure Systems and Software Laboratory at the University of California, Irvine.\nSCONCE - Secure Computing and Networking Center   SCONCE focuses on research for protecting information and computing infrastructure with an emphasis in areas like applied cryptography, network security and information assurance.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore faculty \xc2\xbb\n\nResearch areas\nResearch centers\nResearch highlights\n\nQuick Links \n           \n\nCopyright Inquiries |\n   UCI Directory |\n   Intranet |\n   \n src=\'/bin/icssearchstyle/js/icssearchform.js\' type=\'text/javascript\'></script>\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    </div>\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n<!-- before breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/">Faculty</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/centers/">Research centers</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/">Faculty</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/faculty/centers/">Research centers</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">ICS Research Centers</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<img alt="ICS faculty member" height="150" hspace="5" src="ics-research-centers.jpg" style="float: right;" width="200"/>\n<p>Organized research programs provide a mechanism and organizational structure within which collective research activities can take place that are fundamentally different from those that occur normally within the schools and departments. They are intended to foster the development of short- and long-term research programs that span disciplines and academic units, thereby making it possible for faculty to acquire extramural resources for which they might not otherwise qualify. The following is a list of the research centers that are part of ICS:</p>\n<p><a href="http://abrc.uci.edu">ABRC - Ada Byron Research Center</a> <br/> ABRC studies and promotes diverse access to and participation in computer science, engineering, digital media and related information technology fields.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.calit2.uci.edu">Calit2 - California Institute for Telecommunications and Information Technology</a> <br/> A multidisciplinary research institute in collaboration with UCSD, Calit2@UCI integrates academic research with industry experience to seek innovative IT approaches that will benefit society and ignite economic development.</p>\n<p><a href="http://merage.uci.edu/ResearchAndCenters/CDT/">CDT - Center for Digital Transformation</a><a href="http://www.crito.uci.edu/"><br/></a>One of the world\'s leading think tanks on the impact of information technology on organizations and society and on the management of information technology.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7etheory/">Center for Algorithms and Theory of Computation</a> <br/> The goal of research in theoretical computer science is to produce results, supported by rigorous proof, about problems dealing with computers and their applications.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.cecs.uci.edu/">Center for Embedded Computer Systems</a> <br/> Conducting leading-edge interdisciplinary research in embedded systems, the center develops innovative design methodologies, and promote technology and knowledge transfer for the benefit of the individual and society.</p>\n<p><a href="http://cml.ics.uci.edu/">Center for Machine Learning and Intelligent Systems</a> <br/> Addresses the challenges of the modern data-driven world, using computer algorithms to discover useful information from vast data archives.</p>\n<!-- --> <!-- -->\n<p><strong>Center for Social Computing</strong><br/>Conducts foundational research into the relationship between information technology and society. Based at UCI, the center brings together an interdisciplinary group of researchers from leading U.S. universities.</p>\n<!-- --> <!-- -->\n<p><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7eprojects/cert/">CERT - Center for Emergency Response Technologies</a> <br/> Works to radically transform the ability of responding organizations to gather, manage, use, and disseminate information within emergency response networks and to the general public. By using more robust information systems, response can focus on activities that have the highest potential to save lives and property.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.cor.web.uci.edu/">COR - Center for Organizational Research</a> <br/> COR contributes to the development of organization theory by connecting scholars from many disciplines who bring their knowledge and methods to a common understanding of these issues.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.cpcc.uci.edu/">CPCC - Center for Pervasive Communications and Computing</a> <br/> Dedicated to serving the vision of wearable computers with wireless connections that enable anyone to have continuous voice, video, and data connectivity.</p>\n<p><a href="http://vision.ics.uci.edu/">Computational Vision Lab<br/> </a>The Computational Vision Lab focuses on understanding the information processing capabilities of biological visual systems and on developing computational systems for processing visual media.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.igb.uci.edu/">IGB - Institute for Genomics and BioInformatics</a> <br/> Fostering innovative basic and applied research in genomics and BioInformatics, IGB works with established companies, start-ups, government agencies and standards bodies to develop and transition these technologies to widespread and practical application.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.isr.uci.edu/">ISR - Institute for Software Research</a> <br/> Works toward advancing software and information technology through research partnerships and educating the next generation of software researchers and practitioners in advanced software technologies.</p>\n<!-- --> <!-- -->\n<p><a href="http://ivecg.uci.edu">IVECG - Institute for Virtual Environments and Computer Games</a><br/> Brings together researchers for the common goal of understanding and creating technology and applications that transform how we: see the world through immersive visualization and virtual tours; interact and socialize with global communities; communicate and collaborate with colleagues in virtual collaborative space; provide medical care and training to remote corners of the world; and educate all ages and populations using virtual environments.</p>\n<!-- --> <!-- -->\n<p><a href="http://luci.ics.uci.edu/">LUCI - Laboratory for Ubiquitous Computing and Interaction</a> <br/> Addresses the entire range of research problems that arise from the ubiquitous computing vision: the design of novel devices, the structure of software systems, techniques for designing and building systems, patterns of interaction, and the cultural implications of ubiquitous computing.</p>\n<p><a href="http://www.ssllab.org/">Secure Systems and Software Laboratory</a> <br/> The Secure Systems and Software Laboratory at the University of California, Irvine.</p>\n<p><a href="http://sconce.ics.uci.edu/">SCONCE - Secure Computing and Networking Center </a> <br/> SCONCE focuses on research for protecting information and computing infrastructure with an emphasis in areas like applied cryptography, network security and information assurance.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div id="sidebar_title">More faculty &#187;</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="../area/index.php">Research areas</a></li>\n<li><a href="index.php">Research centers</a></li>\n<li><a \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    Bren school home > Faculty > Research highlights\n \nResearch highlights\n\n\nEvery day, our faculty and students make important research contributions that bring real and positive change to people worldwide.\nBelow are examples of the life-changing work conducted at the Bren School of ICS.\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\nAdaptive Software and Hardware for Distributed, Networked Embedded SystemsAlgorithmic LivingApplying Machine Learning and Advanced Computation to CancerAsterixDB: Big Data Management 2.0CloudProtectCollaboration Success WizardFault ComprehensionGene Regulation Network (GRN) InferenceMachine Learning for Text and Social Network Data over TimeModeling Languages for Computational Biology and AIModeling and Simulation of Biologically-Realistic Brain NetworksMulti-tasking in the WorkplaceRobust and Flexible Statistical Models for Environmental Epidemiology StudiesSatwareSherlockSimilarity-based Program AnalysisSoftware Engineering for SustainabilityStatistical Models for Brain ConnectivityTechnologies for Autism: Activity CoachThe I-Sensorium ProjectTrust in Software Development TeamsValues in DesignWebRTC Benchmarking and OptimizationAdaptive Software and Hardware for Distributed, Networked Embedded SystemsThe project investigates adaptive strategies to deal with dynamic application environments for distributed, networked embedded systems, covering diverse applications such as the Internet-of-Things low-power mobile systems.Department of Computer ScienceAlgorithmic LivingAll of the data collected about us is used to make decisions about what sort of products and financial offers we receive. How does this manifest in our self-image, and what are the historical and legal implications?Department of InformaticsApplying Machine Learning and Advanced Computation to CancerIn this project, researchers have identified an elusive pocket on the surface of the p53 protein that can be targeted by cancer-fighting drugs.Department of Computer ScienceAsterixDB: Big Data Management 2.0AsterixDB is a full-function, open-source, next-generation Big Data Management System that is designed to scale to very large shared clusters.Department of Computer ScienceCloudProtectCloudProtect seeks to develop a middleware so users can employ encryption methods to control risk of data exposure in Cloud-based applications.Department of Computer ScienceCollaboration Success WizardThis online diagnostic survey looks at how to improve collaborations on projects where workers are spread out geographically. The survey probes factors that may strengthen or weaken the collaboration and provides reports that help build productive collaborations.Department of InformaticsFault ComprehensionWhen software fails it must be "debugged," a largely manual process that determines why the program failed. This project is creating tools and visualizations that give an automated diagnosis to help software developers create effective and efficient software.Department of InformaticsGene Regulation Network (GRN) InferenceIn collaboration with UCI biologists, researchers will use their pioneering GRN mathematical models along with machine learning-based inference methods to computationally understand the gene-regulation network that determines early endoderm patterning in vertebrates.Department of Computer ScienceMachine Learning for Text and Social Network Data over TimeResearchers are developing new statistical machine learning algorithms that can automatically extract useful information from both large bodies of and large social network data sets.Department of Computer ScienceModeling Languages for Computational Biology and AIThis project seeks to exploit useful overlap between formally defined scientific modeling languages researchers have developed for computational biology, including machine-learning techniques for model reduction.Department of Computer ScienceModeling and Simulation of Biologically-Realistic Brain NetworksIn collaboration with neuroscientists, this project develops modeling and simulation frameworks for exploring large spiking neural networks, with a specific focus on visually guided motion perception, learning, tracking and autonomous navigation.Department of Computer ScienceMulti-tasking in the WorkplaceModern technology has helped create workplaces filled with interruptions, influencing work flow and productivity. \xc2\xa0This project studies information workers to figure out ways of mitigating the impact of constant interruptions.Department of InformaticsRobust and Flexible Statistical Models for Environmental Epidemiology StudiesResearchers are developing new statistical methods to flexibly estimate the association between spatially and/or temporally correlated environmental exposures and the risk of clinical outcomes in humans.Department of StatisticsSatwareThis scalable data collection, querying and analysis technology allows for the creation of situational awareness applications from across diverse, multimodal sensors and data sources.Department of Computer ScienceSherlockA pay-as-you-go data cleaning framework, Sherlock can improve data quality in (near) real-time application contexts.Department of Computer ScienceSimilarity-based Program AnalysisThis project explores the idea of using "program similarity" to find better heuristics that require a lot less time and effort to find a solution. Program similarity can be defined in a number of ways and part of this research is seeking to find intrinsic program characteristics that can be used for this purpose.Department of Computer ScienceSoftware Engineering for SustainabilityThere is growing awareness that living within the Earth\'s means is crucial to humanity. This sustainability has been focused on engineering advances to reduce waste and energy use. But information and computing technology could also play a key role. This project seeks to understand the potential of information technology in helping people make smarter decisions and ways in which to make IT software more sustainable.Department of InformaticsStatistical Models for Brain ConnectivityUnder the context of decision making, this project seeks to develop novel statistical approaches for identifying brain connectivity features from high dimensional multimodal imaging spatio-temporal data that can predict human behavior.Department of StatisticsTechnologies for Autism: Activity CoachFor many people living with autism spectrum disorder, remembering detailed schedules can be a challenge. A well planned day can be disrupted by a late bus or cancelled work. ActivityCoach, a mobile application, provides support that adapts to changing schedules.Department of InformaticsThe I-Sensorium ProjectParts of the UCI campus are equipped with a variety of experimental sensing, networking, storage and computing technologies to convert the campus into a "living laboratory." Data from I-Sensorium infrastructure is driving experimental research on pervasive systems, mobile computing, situation awareness, big data management, data streams, multimodal event detection and privacy.Department of Computer ScienceTrust in Software Development TeamsTeams that are productive tend to have a great amount of trust among the team members. In virtual teams, trust is difficult to establish. This project explores how trust is formed among team members, and it\'s creating tools to help teams that are spread out geographically develop trust.Department of InformaticsValues in DesignThis project seeks to understand the personal and cultural values we design into our technologies, and how these technologies allow us to express our values. For example, how do we balance values of efficiency and security with a need for friendliness and fun when we design a new electronic marketplace?Department of InformaticsWebRTC Benchmarking and OptimizationWebRTC is an exciting new standard being developed to provide real-time communication capabilities between browsers. It is a major component of the HTML5, the newest version of HTML protocol under development today. This project develops methodology and software for performing multi-platform, browser-independent performance benchmarking. The benchmarking results will be used to optimize and improve WebRTC performance on mobile devices.Department of Computer Science\n\n\n\n   \n   Quick Links \n      \n      \n\n\n\n         \n      \n sfHover);\r\n\r\n</script>\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n      <style>\r\n\r\n\r\n         #school_header {\r\n             background-image: href=\'https://duttgroup.ics.uci.edu/doku.php/projects\'><SPAN>Adaptive Software and Hardware for Distributed, Networked Embedded Systems</SPAN></A><a class=\'c15\' href=\'http://socialcomputing.uci.edu/content/research-themes\'><SPAN>Algorithmic Living</SPAN></A><a class=\'c1\' href=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/community/news/press/view_press?id=122\'><SPAN>Applying Machine Learning and Advanced Computation to Cancer</SPAN></A><a class=\'c2\' href=\'http://asterix.ics.uci.edu\'><SPAN>AsterixDB: Big Data Management 2.0</SPAN></A><a class=\'c3\' (GRN) Inference</SPAN></A><a class=\'c6\' href=\'http://www.datalab.uci.edu/papers/\'><SPAN>Machine Learning for Text and Social Network Data over Time</SPAN></A><a class=\'c8\' href=\'http://emj.ics.uci.edu/papers/machine-learning-papers/\'><SPAN>Modeling Languages for Computational Biology and AI</SPAN></A><a class=\'c7\' href=\'https://duttgroup.ics.uci.edu/doku.php/projects\'><SPAN>Modeling and Simulation of Biologically-Realistic Brain Networks</SPAN></A><a class=\'c18\' href=\'http://ics.uci.edu/%7Egmark/Home_page/Research.html\'><SPAN>Multi-tasking in the Workplace</SPAN></A><a class=\'c13\' href=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7edgillen\'><SPAN>Robust and Flexible
