href=\'http://sherlock.ics.uci.edu\'><SPAN>Sherlock</SPAN></A><a class=\'c11\' href=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7esysarch/\'><SPAN>Similarity-based Program Analysis</SPAN></A><a class=\'c19\' href=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7Edjr/DebraJRichardson/SE4S.html\'><SPAN>Software Engineering for Sustainability</SPAN></A><a class=\'c14\' href=\'http://hombao.ics.uci.edu/\'><SPAN>Statistical Models for Brain Connectivity</SPAN></A><a class=\'c20\' href=\'http://star-uci.org/2012/09/29/technologies-for-autism-activitycoach\'><SPAN>Technologies for Autism: Activity Coach</SPAN></A><a class=\'c5\' href=\'http://www.i-sensorium.org\'><SPAN>The I-Sensorium Project</SPAN></A><a class=\'c21\' href=\'#\'><SPAN>Trust in Software Development Teams</SPAN></A><a class=\'c22\' href=\'http://evoke.ics.uci.edu/research/values-in-design\'><SPAN>Values in Design</SPAN></A><a class=\'c12\' href=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7esysarch/\'><SPAN>WebRTC Benchmarking and Optimization</SPAN></A></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'projects-hover-descriptions\'><DIV CLASS=\'desc c0\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'https://duttgroup.ics.uci.edu/doku.php/projects\'>Adaptive Software and Hardware for Distributed, Networked Embedded Systems</A></B><P>The project investigates adaptive strategies to deal with dynamic application environments for distributed, networked embedded systems, covering diverse applications such as the Internet-of-Things low-power mobile systems.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c15\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://socialcomputing.uci.edu/content/research-themes\'>Algorithmic Living</A></B><P>All of the data collected about us is used to make decisions about what sort of products and financial offers we receive. How does this manifest in our self-image, and what are the historical and legal implications?<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c1\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/community/news/press/view_press?id=122\'>Applying Machine Learning and Advanced Computation to Cancer</A></B><P>In this project, researchers have identified an elusive pocket on the surface of the p53 protein that can be targeted by cancer-fighting drugs.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c2\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://asterix.ics.uci.edu\'>AsterixDB: Big Data Management 2.0</A></B><P>AsterixDB is a full-function, open-source, next-generation Big Data Management System that is designed to scale to very large shared clusters.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c3\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://radicle.ics.uci.edu\'>CloudProtect</A></B><P>CloudProtect seeks to develop a middleware so users can employ encryption methods to control risk of data exposure in Cloud-based applications.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c16\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'#\'>Collaboration Success Wizard</A></B><P>This online diagnostic survey looks at how to improve collaborations on projects where workers are spread out geographically. The survey probes factors that may strengthen or weaken the collaboration and provides reports that help build productive collaborations.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c17\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://spideruci.org/fault-comprehension\'>Fault Comprehension</A></B><P>When software fails it must be "debugged," a largely manual process that determines why the program failed. This project is creating tools and visualizations that give an automated diagnosis to help software developers create effective and efficient software.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c4\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://emj.ics.uci.edu/papers/computational-biology-papers/\'>Gene Regulation Network (GRN) Inference</A></B><P>In collaboration with UCI biologists, researchers will use their pioneering GRN mathematical models along with machine learning-based inference methods to computationally understand the gene-regulation network that determines early endoderm patterning in vertebrates.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c6\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.datalab.uci.edu/papers/\'>Machine Learning for Text and Social Network Data over Time</A></B><P>Researchers are developing new statistical machine learning algorithms that can automatically extract useful information from both large bodies of and large social network data sets.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c8\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://emj.ics.uci.edu/papers/machine-learning-papers/\'>Modeling Languages for Computational Biology and AI</A></B><P>This project seeks to exploit useful overlap between formally defined scientific modeling languages researchers have developed for computational biology, including machine-learning techniques for model reduction.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c7\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'https://duttgroup.ics.uci.edu/doku.php/projects\'>Modeling and Simulation of Biologically-Realistic Brain Networks</A></B><P>In collaboration with neuroscientists, this project develops modeling and simulation frameworks for exploring large spiking neural networks, with a specific focus on visually guided motion perception, learning, tracking and autonomous navigation.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c18\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://ics.uci.edu/%7Egmark/Home_page/Research.html\'>Multi-tasking in the Workplace</A></B><P>Modern technology has helped create workplaces filled with interruptions, influencing work flow and productivity. &#160;This project studies information workers to figure out ways of mitigating the impact of constant interruptions.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c13\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7edgillen\'>Robust and Flexible Statistical Models for Environmental Epidemiology Studies</A></B><P>Researchers are developing new statistical methods to flexibly estimate the association between spatially and/or temporally correlated environmental exposures and the risk of clinical outcomes in humans.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Statistics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c9\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7eprojects/satware\'>Satware</A></B><P>This scalable data collection, querying and analysis technology allows for the creation of situational awareness applications from across diverse, multimodal sensors and data sources.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c10\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://sherlock.ics.uci.edu\'>Sherlock</A></B><P>A pay-as-you-go data cleaning framework, Sherlock can improve data quality in (near) real-time application contexts.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c11\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7esysarch/\'>Similarity-based Program Analysis</A></B><P>This project explores the idea of using "program similarity" to find better heuristics that require a lot less time and effort to find a solution. Program similarity can be defined in a number of ways and part of this research is seeking to find intrinsic program characteristics that can be used for this purpose.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c19\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7Edjr/DebraJRichardson/SE4S.html\'>Software Engineering for Sustainability</A></B><P>There is growing awareness that living within the Earth\'s means is crucial to humanity. This sustainability has been focused on engineering advances to reduce waste and energy use. But information and computing technology could also play a key role. This project seeks to understand the potential of information technology in helping people make smarter decisions and ways in which to make IT software more sustainable.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c14\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://hombao.ics.uci.edu/\'>Statistical Models for Brain Connectivity</A></B><P>Under the context of decision making, this project seeks to develop novel statistical approaches for identifying brain connectivity features from high dimensional multimodal imaging spatio-temporal data that can predict human behavior.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Statistics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c20\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://star-uci.org/2012/09/29/technologies-for-autism-activitycoach\'>Technologies for Autism: Activity Coach</A></B><P>For many people living with autism spectrum disorder, remembering detailed schedules can be a challenge. A well planned day can be disrupted by a late bus or cancelled work. ActivityCoach, a mobile application, provides support that adapts to changing schedules.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c5\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.i-sensorium.org\'>The I-Sensorium Project</A></B><P>Parts of the UCI campus are equipped with a variety of experimental sensing, networking, storage and computing technologies to convert the campus into a "living laboratory." Data from I-Sensorium infrastructure is driving experimental research on pervasive systems, mobile computing, situation awareness, big data management, data streams, multimodal event detection and privacy.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c21\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'#\'>Trust in Software Development Teams</A></B><P>Teams that are productive tend to have a great amount of trust among the team members. In virtual teams, trust is difficult to establish. This project explores how trust is formed among team members, and it\'s creating tools to help teams that are spread out geographically develop trust.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c22\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://evoke.ics.uci.edu/research/values-in-design\'>Values in Design</A></B><P>This project seeks to understand the personal and cultural values we design into our technologies, and how these technologies allow us to express our values. For example, how do we balance values of efficiency and security with a need for friendliness and fun when we design a new electronic marketplace?<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Informatics</P></DIV><DIV CLASS=\'desc c12\' STYLE=\'display: none; \'><P><B><A HREF=\'http://www.ics.uci.edu/%7esysarch/\'>WebRTC Benchmarking and Optimization</A></B><P>WebRTC is an exciting new standard being developed to provide real-time communication capabilities between browsers. It is a major component of the HTML5, the newest version of HTML protocol under development today. This project develops methodology and software for performing multi-platform, browser-independent performance benchmarking. The benchmarking results will be used to optimize and improve WebRTC performance on mobile devices.<P STYLE=\'font-size: 90%; font-style: italic; \'>Department of Computer Science</P></DIV></DIV></DIV></div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="links_bottom"><div style="float: left; margin-right: 1em; notmargin-left: 1em; border: 0px dotted grey;">\n   <form students studying virtually every principle area within the fields of Computer Science, Informatics, Networked Systems, Software Engineering and Statistics, as well as many new interdisciplinary topics. With more than 75 faculty members spanning three departments\xe2\x80\x94Computer Science, Informatics and Statistics\xe2\x80\x94a state-of-the-art 90,000 sq. ft. building and a $20 million gift from philanthropist Donald Bren, this is a very exciting time to be a part of the Donald Bren School.\nAlmost all of our Ph.D. students receive financial aid in the form of teaching assistantships or research assistantships during their time at UC Irvine. Many of them also receive fellowships from the Bren School's corporate partners and private supporters.\nYou can still apply to ICS if your undergraduate degree is not in the same area as the graduate degree in which you are interested. However, it is helpful if you have taken courses in computer science and math, and/or have some related work experience.\nA complete list of our graduate programs is below so you can explore which one is right for you.\xc2\xa0You can also visit the\xc2\xa0UCI Course Catalog\xc2\xa0for more in-depth information about each ICS graduate program.\nICS Graduate Programs of id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Prospective Graduate Students</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<h2 class="header"><img alt="Students studying" height="200" src="../../bin/img/photos/degrees/bmi_header.jpg" style="float: right;" width="156"/>Your Success Starts at ICS</h2>\n<p>Join more than 400 graduate students studying virtually every principle area within the fields of Computer Science, Informatics, Networked Systems, Software Engineering and Statistics, as well as many new interdisciplinary topics. With more than 75 faculty members spanning three departments&#8212;Computer Science, Informatics and Statistics&#8212;a state-of-the-art 90,000 sq. ft. building and a $20 million gift from philanthropist Donald Bren, this is a very exciting time to be a part of the Donald Bren School.</p>\nAlmost all of our Ph.D. students receive financial aid in the form of teaching assistantships or research assistantships during their time at UC Irvine. Many of them also receive fellowships from the Bren School\'s corporate partners and private supporters.\n<p>You can still apply to ICS if your undergraduate degree is not in the same area as the graduate degree in which you are interested. However, it is helpful if you have taken courses in computer science and math, and/or have some related work experience.</p>\n<p>A complete list of our graduate programs is below so you can explore which one is right for you.&#160;<span>You can also visit the&#160;</span><a href="http://catalogue.uci.edu/donaldbrenschoolofinformationandcomputersciences/#graduatetext" target="_blank">UCI Course Catalog</a><span>&#160;for more in-depth information about each ICS graduate program.</span></p>\n<h3>ICS Graduate Programs of Study</h3>\n<p><strong>&#187;&#160;Computer Science&#160;&#8212;&#160;</strong><a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/degree_cs.php">Ph.D.</a>&#160;&#160;l &#160;<a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/degree_cs.php">M.S.</a><a        \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Graduate > Admissions\n\n\n  \nGraduate Application Process\n\n\n\n\nOnline applications for graduate admissions are accepted from September 1st to December 15th. All materials as outlined below should be submitted before the December 15th deadline. (Additional information for those re-applying to the Bren School can be found here.)\nYou can still apply to ICS if your undergraduate degree is not in the same area as the graduate degree in which you are interested. However, it is helpful if you have taken courses in computer science and math, and/or have some related work experience.\nICS accepts applications for admission beginning in the fall quarter only.\n\xc2\xbb Online Application\nComplete the online application. Pay particular attention to the following:\n\nEnter the appropriate codes for ICS. Note that you must choose either M.S. or Ph.D. as ICS does not have a M.S./Ph.D. program.\n\n\n\nComputer Science, Ph.D.\nComputer Science, M.S.\nInformatics, Ph.D.\nNetworked Systems, Ph.D.\nNetworked Systems, M.S.\nSoftware Engineering, Ph.D.\nSoftware Engineering, M.S.\nStatistics, Ph.D.\nStatistics, M.S.\nInformation and Computer Science,\xc2\xa0M.S.\n\n\n\nEnter a specific area of interest. More information about research areas can be found here.\nSave your application ID and student ID numbers; they will be asked of you when filling out other documents.\nApplications are processed after the application fee ($90 for domestic applicants, $110 for foreign applicants) has been received. The application fee canot be waived.\nYou can apply for more than one program simultaneously, but you must fill out a separate application and pay a separate fee for each program.\nIf you have questions regarding your electronic application or your payment, contact UCI Graduate Division at (949) 824-4611 or ogs@uci.edu.\xc2\xa0\n\n\xc2\xbb GRE and TOEFL Scores\nArrange to have your official test scores sent from the testing agency to UC Irvine. Photocopies or scans will not be accepted.\nGRE\n\nThe General GRE is required of ALL applicants.\nFor official GRE General test scores, use Institutional code: 4859\nThere is no minimum GRE score.\nThe Computer Science Subject GRE is recommended for applicants who do not have a degree in Computer Science or a related field.\nGRE scores are good for five years, after which time the exam must be retaken.\nWe cannot accept GMAT scores in lieu of GRE scores.\n\n\nTOEFL\n\nThe TOEFL (Test of English as a Foreign Language) is required of international applicants.\nFor official TOEFL test scores, use Institutional code: 4859\nThe minimum TOEFL score is 80. For more information, please see Graduate Division's English Proficiency site.\nUCI will only waive the TOEFL requirement for applicants who have completed ALL requirements for a B.S., M.S. or Ph.D. degree in the U.S. prior to submitting their application.\n\n\xc2\xbb Letters of Recommendation\nThree letters of recommendation are required, but you may submit as many letters as you wish.\nFor paper submission\nProvide the Letter of Recommendation and Waiver of Access forms to at least three people you have identified who can evaluate your academic and/or professional achievements, describe your strengths and weaknesses and comment on your character, integrity and motivation. Your recommenders should mail his/her letter directly to:\nICS Graduate OfficeDonald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences352 Information & Computer Science Bldg.University of California, IrvineIrvine, CA 92697-3430\nFor online submission\nApplicants who have completed and submitted their online application should send their recommenders a link to that page, along with their application ID number.\n\xc2\xbb Personal Statement\nThe Personal Statement (same as Statement of Purpose) should be submitted via the online application.\n\xc2\xbb Official Transcripts\nArrange to have one copy of your official transcripts from the colleges you attended sent directly to the ICS Graduate Office.\nAn official English translation is required from international students.\nPhotocopies, scans, or unofficial copies of transcripts will not be accepted.\n\xc2\xbb Checking Your Application Status\nApplicants may login to the online GATS TRACKER to check for application materials received and their current application status.\nPh.D. and M.S. admissions decisions are ongoing from approximately March through May. Acceptance and denial letters will be sent electronically.\nWe cannot provide you with the final decision over the phone.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore Graduate \xc2\xbb\n\nContact\nProspective students\nHow to Apply\nPrograms of study\n\nM.S. degree overview\nPh.D. degree overview\n\n\nAcademic year plan\nForms\nPolicies\nFunding & housing\nComputing support\nCampus resources\nVisit the Bren breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/admissions/">Admissions</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/admissions/">Admissions</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Graduate Application Process</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p>Online applications for graduate admissions are accepted from September 1st to December 15th. All materials as outlined below should be submitted <strong>before the December 15th deadline</strong>. (Additional information for those re-applying to the Bren School can be found <a href="Prospective_Re-applying.php" target="_blank" title="ICS Student Affairs: Re-applying for Graduate Program">here</a>.)</p>\n<p>You can still apply to ICS if your undergraduate degree is not in the same area as the graduate degree in which you are interested. However, it is helpful if you have taken courses in computer science and math, and/or have some related work experience.</p>\n<p><em>ICS accepts applications for admission beginning in the fall quarter only</em>.</p>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Online Application</strong></h3>\n<p>Complete the <a href="https://apps.grad.uci.edu/ogsa//index.cfm?action=log_in&amp;CFID=13244617&amp;CFTOKEN=90684455" target="_blank" title="Applicaton for Graduate Admission">online application</a>. Pay particular attention to the following:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Enter the appropriate codes for ICS. Note that <em>you must choose either M.S. or Ph.D.</em> as ICS does not have a M.S./Ph.D. program.</li>\n</ul>\n<blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li type="circle">Computer Science, <strong>Ph.D.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Computer Science, <strong>M.S.<br/></strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Informatics, <strong>Ph.D.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Networked Systems, <strong>Ph.D.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Networked Systems, <strong>M.S.<br/></strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Software Engineering, <strong>Ph.D.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Software Engineering, <strong>M.S.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Statistics, <strong>Ph.D.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Statistics, <strong>M.S.</strong></li>\n<li type="circle">Information and Computer Science,&#160;<strong>M.S.</strong></li>\n</ul>\n</blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li>Enter a specific area of interest. More information about research areas can be found <a href="../../faculty/area/index.php">here</a>.</li>\n<li>Save your application ID and student ID numbers; they will be asked of you when filling out other documents.</li>\n<li>Applications are processed after the application fee ($90 for domestic applicants, $110 for foreign applicants) has been received. The application fee canot be waived.</li>\n<li>You can apply for more than one program simultaneously, but you must fill out a separate application and pay a separate fee for each program.</li>\n<li>If you have questions regarding your electronic application or your payment, contact UCI Graduate Division at (949) 824-4611 or <a href="mailto:ogs@uci.edu">ogs@uci.edu</a>.&#160;</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> GRE and TOEFL Scores</strong></h3>\n<p>Arrange to have your official test scores sent from the testing agency to UC Irvine. Photocopies or scans will not be accepted.</p>\n<p><strong><em>GRE</em></strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The General GRE is required of ALL applicants.</li>\n<li>For official GRE General test scores, use <strong>Institutional code: 4859</strong></li>\n<li>There is no minimum GRE score.</li>\n<li>The Computer Science Subject GRE is recommended for applicants who do not have a degree in Computer Science or a related field.</li>\n<li>GRE scores are good for five years, after which time the exam must be retaken.</li>\n<li>We cannot accept GMAT scores in lieu of GRE scores.</li>\n</ul>\n<blockquote/>\n<p><strong><em>TOEFL</em></strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>The TOEFL (Test of English as a Foreign Language) is required of international applicants.</li>\n<li>For official TOEFL test scores, use <strong>Institutional code: 4859</strong></li>\n<li>The minimum TOEFL score is 80. For more information, please see <a href="http://www.grad.uci.edu/admissions/applying-to-uci/english-proficiency.html" target="_blank" title="Graduate Division English Proficiency">Graduate Division\'s English Proficiency site</a>.</li>\n<li>UCI will only waive the TOEFL requirement for applicants who have completed ALL requirements for a B.S., M.S. or Ph.D. degree in the U.S. prior to submitting their application.</li>\n</ul>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Letters of Recommendation</strong></h3>\n<p><em>Three</em> letters of recommendation are required, but you may submit as many letters as you wish.</p>\n<p><strong><em>For paper submission</em></strong></p>\n<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Provide the Letter of Recommendation and Waiver of Access forms to at least three people you have identified who can evaluate your academic and/or professional achievements, describe your strengths and weaknesses and comment on your character, integrity and motivation. Your recommenders should mail his/her letter directly to:</p>\n<p style="padding-left: 50px;">ICS Graduate Office<br/>Donald Bren School of Information and Computer Sciences<br/>352 Information &amp; Computer Science Bldg.<br/>University of California, Irvine<br/>Irvine, CA 92697-3430</p>\n<p><strong><em>For online submission</em></strong></p>\n<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Applicants who have completed and submitted their online application should send their recommenders a link to that page, along with their application ID number.</p>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Personal Statement</strong></h3>\n<p>The Personal Statement (same as Statement of Purpose) should be submitted via the online application.</p>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Official Transcripts</strong></h3>\n<p>Arrange to have one copy of your official transcripts from the colleges you attended sent directly to the ICS Graduate Office.</p>\n<p>An official English translation is required from international students.</p>\n<p>Photocopies, scans, or unofficial copies of transcripts will not be accepted.</p>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Checking Your Application Status</strong></h3>\n<p>Applicants may login to the online <a href="https://gats.ics.uci.edu//tracker/" target="_blank" title="GATS Tracker">GATS TRACKER</a> to check for application materials received and their current application status.</p>\n<p>Ph.D. and M.S. admissions decisions are ongoing from approximately March through May. Acceptance and denial letters will be sent electronically.</p>\n<p>We cannot provide you with the final decision over the phone.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div        \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Graduate > Degrees\n\n\n  \nOverview of ICS M.S. Programs\n\n\n\n\nICS offers M.S. degrees in Computer Science, Information and Computer Science, Software Engineering, Networked Systems, and Statistics.\xc2\xa0The objective of the terminal M.S. degree is to prepare students for a variety of advanced careers in the computing industry (e.g., software development, information technology consulting, application specific integrated circuit design, network design and configuration, embedded systems design, algorithms development, data mining). The Master's program can be pursued full- or part-time, and required courses may be taken during the first and second year of study. The degree should take no longer than two years if pursued full-time.\n\n\xc2\xbb M.S. Exams and Reviews\nGraduate Student Review\nAt the end of each spring quarter, a formal review is conducted of all M.S. students. If unsatisfactory progress is being made, a letter of probation will be sent to the student and placed in their file. The probation period varies, depending on each student's academic situation. If the problem is not cleared during the probation period, the ICS Graduate Office may recommend dismissal from the program. It is the student's responsibility to make sure the ICS Graduate Office is aware of any problem that has been cleared during the probation period.\nAdvancing to Candidacy for the M.S. Degree\nAdvancement to candidacy implies that a student is almost finished with his/her degree requirements. This is not an automatic process. The students is responsible for making sure his or her form is completed and gets filed. The Advancement to Candidacy should be submitted at least one quarter before the student plans on graduating.\nComprehensive Exam (Option 1)\nStudents who elect for the Comprehensive Exam option must pass a comprehensive examination offered by the department or by a representative of the specific research area. Students should speak to the ICS Graduate Counselor or research area representative regarding test dates, preparation, and reading lists. The faculty within the particular area develops the exam; this may result in the content and structure varying from year to year.\nThesis Option (Option 2)\nThe thesis option is available to all Bren School M.S. students, except for those in the Statistics Program, who do not plan to take the comprehensive exam and who are in good academic standing with the School. Students pursuing this option must enroll in at least two quarters of Thesis Supervision, which will substitute for two required courses as specified under the concentration area or track of choice. A committee will guide the student and give final approval of the thesis. An oral presentation of the thesis to the committee is required.\n\xc2\xa0\n\xc2\xbb Degree Conferral\nThe M.S. degree will be conferred by the UCI Graduate Division the quarter following advancement to candidacy if all degree requirements are satisfied. Graduate Division will send a letter of degree confirmation. Diplomas will be ready for pick up from the Registrar's Office about four months after graduation.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore Graduate \xc2\xbb\n\nContact\nProspective students\nHow to Apply\nPrograms of breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/">Degrees</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/">Degrees</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Overview of ICS M.S. Programs</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p>ICS offers M.S. degrees in Computer Science, Information and Computer Science, Software Engineering, Networked Systems, and Statistics.&#160;The objective of the terminal M.S. degree is to prepare students for a variety of advanced careers in the computing industry (e.g., software development, information technology consulting, application specific integrated circuit design, network design and configuration, embedded systems design, algorithms development, data mining). The Master\'s program can be pursued full- or part-time, and required courses may be taken during the first and second year of study. The degree should take no longer than two years if pursued full-time.</p>\n<hr style="width: 100%;" width="100%"/>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> M.S. Exams and Reviews</strong></h3>\n<p><strong><em>Graduate Student Review</em></strong></p>\n<p>At the end of each spring quarter, a formal review is conducted of all M.S. students. If unsatisfactory progress is being made, a letter of probation will be sent to the student and placed in their file. The probation period varies, depending on each student\'s academic situation. If the problem is not cleared during the probation period, the ICS Graduate Office may recommend dismissal from the program. It is the student\'s responsibility to make sure the ICS Graduate Office is aware of any problem that has been cleared during the probation period.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Advancing to Candidacy for the M.S. Degree</em></strong></p>\n<p>Advancement to candidacy implies that a student is almost finished with his/her degree requirements. This is not an automatic process. The students is responsible for making sure his or her form is completed and gets filed. The Advancement to Candidacy should be submitted at least one quarter before the student plans on graduating.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Comprehensive Exam (Option 1)</em></strong></p>\n<p>Students who elect for the Comprehensive Exam option must pass a comprehensive examination offered by the department or by a representative of the specific research area. Students should speak to the ICS Graduate Counselor or research area representative regarding test dates, preparation, and reading lists. The faculty within the particular area develops the exam; this may result in the content and structure varying from year to year.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Thesis Option (Option 2)</em></strong></p>\n<p>The thesis option is available to all Bren School M.S. students, except for those in the Statistics Program, who do not plan to take the comprehensive exam and who are in good academic standing with the School. Students pursuing this option must enroll in at least two quarters of Thesis Supervision, which will substitute for two required courses as specified under the concentration area or track of choice. A committee will guide the student and give final approval of the thesis. An oral presentation of the thesis to the committee is required.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Degree Conferral</strong></h3>\nThe M.S. degree will be conferred by the UCI Graduate Division the quarter following advancement to candidacy if all degree requirements are satisfied. Graduate Division will send a letter of degree confirmation. Diplomas will be ready for pick up from the Registrar\'s Office about four months after graduation.\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div id="sidebar_title">More Graduate        \r\n                \r\n\r\n\r\n                 \r\n                                 \r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n            \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n    \n\nBren school home > Graduate > Degrees\n\n\n  \nOverview of ICS Ph.D. Programs\n\n\n\n\nICS offers Ph.D. degrees in Computer Science, Information and Computer Science, Software Engineering, Networked Systems and Statistics.\xc2\xa0These Ph.D. programs are research-oriented and encourage students to collaborate with faculty to solve advanced problems in computer science. The programs are full-time and usually take six years to complete. Different degrees/concentrations may have different normative times to degree.\n\n\xc2\xbb Ph.D. Exams and Reviews\nGraduate Student Review\nAt the end of each spring quarter, a formal review is conducted of all Ph.D. students. If unsatisfactory progress is being made, a letter of probation will be sent to the student and placed in their file. The probation period varies, depending on the individual student's academic situation. If the problem is not cleared during the probation period, the ICS Graduate Office may recommend dismissal from the program. It is the student's responsibility to make sure the ICS Graduate Office is aware of any problem that has been cleared during the probation period.\nTeaching Requirement\nAll Ph.D. students are required to participate in teaching activities for two quarters. Summer teaching or teaching at another university may be accepted in fulfillment of this requirement. Students who fulfill this requirement with a teaching assistantship at UCI are required to take an orientation course, ICS 398A, enroll in four units of ICS 399 each quarter they serve as a TA, and attend the TA training program during Welcome Week.\nAdvancing to Candidacy for the M.S.\nPh.D. students can advance to Candidacy for the M.S. degree, unless the student already holds an M.S. degree in Computer Science or a related field. Advancement to candidacy implies that a student is almost finished with his/her degree requirements. Students must advance to candidacy at least one quarter prior to degree conferral.\nStudents with a Previously Earned M.S.\nICS students with an M.S. degree from another university who are working towards their Ph.D. may qualify to receive credit for required courses if their previous M.S. degree was in computer science or a closely related field. Course equivalency will be determined by the ICS Associate Dean for Student Affairs following a written recommendation from the student's advisor. Advisors may require that students take additional courses when appropriate. Final approval will be determined by the Dean of Graduate Division.\nAdvancing to Candidacy for the Ph.D.\nThe advancement exam is an oral presentation to a five-member committee. The student should identify the members who will be on their dissertation committee, obtain the all required signatures, and pay the advancement fee before submitting the candidacy form. When the Dean of Graduate Division has approved advancement, the ICS Graduate Office will notify the student.\nFinal Defense\nFor the final dissertation defense, students should email the ICS Graduate Office with the date, time and location for the defense, the names of their committee members, and the title and abstract of their dissertation. This should be done no less than two weeks before the defense. This information will be sent to all ICS graduate students and faculty. In addition to the student's committee members, anyone else who wishes to attend the defense may do so.\nThe completed dissertation and signed forms is submitted to the UCI Special Collections & Archives in paper or electronic format. Graduate Division will notify students once their degree has been conferred.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore Graduate \xc2\xbb\n\nContact\nProspective students\nHow to Apply\nPrograms of study\n\nM.S. degree breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n<div class="bread" id="breadcrumbs"><!-- starting function breadcrumb_nav --><!-- done with function breadcrumb_nav, going to return [<A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/">Degrees</a>] --><A HREF="/">Bren school home</A> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/">Graduate</a> &gt; <a href="http://www.ics.uci.edu/grad/degrees/">Degrees</a></div>\n<!-- after breadcrumb_nav() print -->\n\n<div id="content"><a id="startcontent" name="startcontent"></a>  \n<div id="content_title">Overview of ICS Ph.D. Programs</div>\n\n<blockquote>\n<div id="content_text">\n\n<p>ICS offers Ph.D. degrees in Computer Science, Information and Computer Science, Software Engineering, Networked Systems and Statistics.&#160;These Ph.D. programs are research-oriented and encourage students to collaborate with faculty to solve advanced problems in computer science. The programs are full-time and usually take six years to complete. Different degrees/concentrations may have different normative times to degree.</p>\n<hr style="width: 100%;" width="100%"/>\n<h3><strong><span style="color: #6699cc;"><strong>&#187;</strong></span> Ph.D. Exams and Reviews</strong></h3>\n<p><strong><em>Graduate Student Review</em></strong></p>\n<p>At the end of each spring quarter, a formal review is conducted of all Ph.D. students. If unsatisfactory progress is being made, a letter of probation will be sent to the student and placed in their file. The probation period varies, depending on the individual student\'s academic situation. If the problem is not cleared during the probation period, the ICS Graduate Office may recommend dismissal from the program. It is the student\'s responsibility to make sure the ICS Graduate Office is aware of any problem that has been cleared during the probation period.</p>\n<strong><em>Teaching Requirement</em></strong>\n<p>All Ph.D. students are required to participate in teaching activities for two quarters. Summer teaching or teaching at another university may be accepted in fulfillment of this requirement. Students who fulfill this requirement with a teaching assistantship at UCI are required to take an orientation course, ICS 398A, enroll in four units of ICS 399 each quarter they serve as a TA, and attend the TA training program during Welcome Week.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Advancing to Candidacy for the M.S.</em></strong></p>\n<p>Ph.D. students can advance to Candidacy for the M.S. degree, unless the student already holds an M.S. degree in Computer Science or a related field. Advancement to candidacy implies that a student is almost finished with his/her degree requirements. Students must advance to candidacy at least one quarter prior to degree conferral.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Students with a Previously Earned M.S.</em></strong></p>\n<p>ICS students with an M.S. degree from another university who are working towards their Ph.D. may qualify to receive credit for required courses if their previous M.S. degree was in computer science or a closely related field. Course equivalency will be determined by the ICS Associate Dean for Student Affairs following a written recommendation from the student\'s advisor. Advisors may require that students take additional courses when appropriate. Final approval will be determined by the Dean of Graduate Division.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Advancing to Candidacy for the Ph.D.</em></strong></p>\n<p>The advancement exam is an oral presentation to a five-member committee. The student should identify the members who will be on their dissertation committee, obtain the all required signatures, and pay the advancement fee before submitting the candidacy form. When the Dean of Graduate Division has approved advancement, the ICS Graduate Office will notify the student.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Final Defense</em></strong></p>\n<p>For the final dissertation defense, students should email the ICS Graduate Office with the date, time and location for the defense, the names of their committee members, and the title and abstract of their dissertation. This should be done no less than two weeks before the defense. This information will be sent to all ICS graduate students and faculty. In addition to the student\'s committee members, anyone else who wishes to attend the defense may do so.</p>\n<p>The completed dissertation and signed forms is submitted to the UCI Special Collections &amp; Archives in paper or electronic format. Graduate Division will notify students once their degree has been conferred.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div id="sidebar_title">More Graduate &#187;</div>\n<ul>\n<li><a opportunities available to ICS Graduate Students are outlined in this PDF document. This is a combined list of those offered by Graduate Division and external sources. Please see the links provided in the document for more information on each fellowship or award.\n*Many fellowships have internal department deadlines 7-10 days prior to the official due date.\nTeaching Assistantships\nStudents can receive funding through appointments as a Teaching Assistant (TA) or Reader. Information on responsibilities, requirements, and benefits can be found on the Graduate Division website here.\nInterested ICS graduate students must submit an application for each quarter they wish to search as a TA or Reader. The application requirement applies to ALL students, including those on a TA/Reader fellowship.\nStudents are notified of their appointments via email as soon as they are assigned. Any questions about TA and Reader assignments should be directed to the Department Managers.\nGraduate Housing\nOn-campus housing is not guaranteed.\nAll students looking for on-campus housing options must apply in order to be considered. Continuing students may apply to the housing waiting list at any time during the year. Admitted students may apply for housing after they submit their Statement of Intent to Register (SIR), and must do so by May 1st.\nContinuing students can find more information on the Student Housing website.\nInformation for new graduate students may be found here.\n\n\n\n\n\nMore Graduate \xc2\xbb\n\nContact\nProspective students\nHow to Apply\nPrograms of study\n\nM.S. degree overview\nPh.D. Students</strong></h3>\n<p>Fellowship and award opportunities available to ICS Graduate Students are outlined in this <a href="GradFellowships.pdf" target="_blank" title="2015 ICS Graduate Fellowships by quarter">PDF document</a>. This is a combined list of those offered by Graduate Division and external sources. Please see the links provided in the document for more information on each fellowship or award.</p>\n<p><em>*Many fellowships have internal department deadlines 7-10 days prior to the official due date.</em></p>\n<h3 class="header">Teaching Assistantships</h3>\n<p>Students can receive funding through appointments as a Teaching Assistant (TA) or Reader. Information on responsibilities, requirements, and benefits can be found on the Graduate Division website <a href="http://www.grad.uci.edu/funding/employment/teaching-assistantships/index.html" target="_blank" title="Graduate Division Teaching Assistantships">here</a>.</p>\n<p>Interested ICS graduate students must submit an application for each quarter they wish to search as a TA or Reader. The application requirement applies to ALL students, including those on a TA/Reader fellowship.</p>\n<p>Students are notified of their appointments via email as soon as they are assigned. Any questions about TA and Reader assignments should be directed to the Department Managers.</p>\n<h3 class="header">Graduate Housing</h3>\n<p>On-campus housing is not guaranteed.</p>\n<p>All students looking for on-campus housing options must apply in order to be considered. Continuing students may apply to the housing waiting list at any time during the year. Admitted students may apply for housing after they submit their Statement of Intent to Register (SIR), and must do so by May 1st.</p>\n<p>Continuing students can find more information on the Student Housing <a href="http://housing.uci.edu/apply/How_To_Apply.html">website</a>.</p>\n<p>Information for new graduate students may be found <a href="http://housing.uci.edu/apply/How_To_Apply.html#newgrads" target="_blank" title="Student Housing New Grads">here</a>.</p>\n\n\n</div>\n</blockquote>\n</div>\n<div id="sidebar"><div
